MOZAMBIQUE
FIRST ROADS AND COASTAL SHIPPING PROJECT
SUMMARY OF ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACTS
A.   ROAD RENABILITATION
1.    The rehabilitation of Mozambican roads which have had little
traffic for many years may involve direct and indirect negative
environmental impacts similar to those of a new road. The direct
impacts that could result from construction-related activities would be
negligible provided that corrective measures are implemented as
recommended in the roads environmental studies. The indirect impacts,
more pertinent to the Project, result from increasing access to areas
which are semi-depopulated, have restricted land use, or which may have
gone through long periods of natural regeneration. They are related not
so much to the road rehabilitation as to the overall process of
development in the area. The extent of the potential indirect impacts
is difficult to ascertain considering the level of information
available. However, they could lead to degradation of important
resources, and have therefore been carefully addressed by the Project.
2.    Indirect Impacts:  Road rehabilitation would provide the
conditions for an increase in traffic and easier access throughout the
regions in question. This, in turn, would create incentive toward
expansion of, particularly, agriculture and timber related activities,
and allow the efficient and uninterrupted transportation of varied
goods, migration, etc. Increasing agriculture could lead to replacement
of existing wooded areas and wetlands, in turn possibly leading to soil
degradation, and loss of current and potential raw materials, and
economically and nutritionally valuable species. Improving transport
efficiency could facilitate transport of vulnerable goods whose
exploitation is presently checked only by the current lack of transport
facilities and security (e.g., timber and fuelwood, and wildlife
products).   Facilitating the transport of vulnerable goods could allow
unsustainable exploitation of timber resources, in turn resulting in
irreversible loss of important economic and ecological resources. While
these goods and activities can be sustainably developed and exploited,
Mozambique is still in the process of developing the basic framework
necessary to do so (including legislative and regulatory, institutional,
technical and human, and financial resources). Hence, unless
appropriate alternatives are provided to existing and incoming
population, and other measures taken to avoid or control the changes in
land use that follow access, depletion of nearby wood resources and
replacement of important pockets of natural vegetation by domestic crops
would follow rehabilitation of the roads.
3.    Conclusions and Recommendations:  The Project in itself would not
be able to prevent or solve the above problem, which is a function of
policies in the forestry and agricultural sectors. However, ROCS-1 and



- 220 -
ANNEX 5-3
Page 2 of 4
subsequent transport projects could contribute to alleviating some of
the above indirect impacts by: (i) helping develop the capacity of the
Mozambican National Environmental Commission (CNA) to participate in and
opportunely provide inputs to the proposed project, and other related
development projects; and (ii) increasing the environmental awareness of
the populations served by the roads. Measures to begin coping with the
indirect negative effects of road rehabilitation civil works to be
carried out under subsequent projects have, therefore, been made an
integral part of ROCS-1.
4.    The Project would provide support and training to CNA to allow it
to begin establishing the capacity necessary to monitor and control
exploitation and transport of wood and wildlife products in the areas
served by the roads. This training would be provided as part of the
programs, policies and procedures CNA is developing to promote
sustainable development of the country's resources, ard coordinated with
training for port environmental agents, to be provided by the coastal
shipping component of the project. This proposal was tentatively
discussed with the Director of the CNA and his team during the
appraisal, and met with their support. Specific measures to facilitate
implementation of the above monitoring were reviewed, and discussions
initiated with other potential donors, particularly the European
Economic Community (EEC), and the United Nations Environmental Program
(UNEP); contacts with the Forestry Department were to be initiated by
CNA. Safety awareness programs proposed for the roads would be combined
with environmental education to provide basic information on soil
conservation, the economic and ecological values of wetlands and forest
resources, and their sustainable development. In addition, road design
in ROCS-1, and rehabilitation civil works in subsequent projects, would
utilize environmentally safe methods and techniques regarding road
construction and related activities.
B. COASTAL SHIPPING
5.    On-going port activities in the small ports under consideration
for rehabilitation and/or improvement under ROCS-1 have, to date,
resulted in direct negative environmental impacts such as water
pollution, and mangrove and estuary ecosystems disturbance, as wc-ll as
the indirect effects of improving coastal shipping of fragile resources,
particularly timber. Port improvements would lead to increased traffic
and related port use, potentially expanding the type and degree of
existing impacts, and adding construction-related negative impacts.
Negative direct impacts from the investments proposed should be
negligible. The negative indirect impacts due to increased economic
activity in the ports, which are difficult to estimate considering the
level of information available, could play a major role in the economic
and environmental well-being of Mozambique. Even though these are not
directly related to the small ports component of the project, ROCS-1 and
subsequent transport improvement projects will include measures to limit
their impact.



- 221 -
ANNEX 5-3
Paae 3 of 4
6.    Indirect Impacts:  Improving the overall efficiency of coastal
shipping would lead to increased capacity at the ports, which in turn
would allow increased product output and increased use of ports by both
small and larger ships. Therefore, the Project would provide the
conditions necessary for an increase in traffic which, in turn, would
facilitate recovery or expansion of, particularly, agriculture and
timber-related activities. Although these activities can be sustainably
developed, Mozambique lacks the framework necessary to counteract their
inherent negative impacts, and is still in the process of developing the
legal, institutional and technical framework and resources essential to
guarantee such development. Hore specifically, Mozambique lacks
appropriate legislation and regulations regarding sustainable
development of forest and agricultural resources, estuary protection,
and pollution standards. In addition, Mozambique has insufficient
financial and human resources to enforce existing forestry regulations,
and lacks enforcement of port regulations concerning water pollution and
mangrove protection. Under these conditions, increased economic
activity as facilitated by the rehabilitation and/or improvement of the
small ports, or of coastal shipping operations, could result in the
increase of indirect negative environmental impacts.
Conclusions and Recommendations:
7.    Although ROCS-1 and subsequent proposed projects involve generally
low levels of improvement, and should not pose any major direct
environmental problem, they could lay the base for further port
development, and hence augment indirect impacts. To control indirect
impacts, and anticipating future development, ROCS-1 would implement the
initial measures necessary to avoid intrinsic negative environmental
impacts. By paying close attention to direct and indirect issues, the
Project wouldt (i) prevent resource degradation and economic losses
within the forestry and fisheries sectors; (ii) halt or prevent
physical degradation of the ports, beaches and port infrastructure;
(iii) prevent economic losses for small privately owned fishing
operations; and (iv) prevent nutrition losses for the poor.
8.    The Project addresses both direct and indirect impacts and
Mozambique's environmental, legal, and institutional framework by: (i)
providing port infrastructure and equipment which do not interfere with
major environmental functions; (ii) including training and technical
assistance to support development of the capacity of CNA to provide
adequate support to the small ports component of the project; (iii)
providing primary equipment and other measures to halt on-going
environmental degradation; and (iv) requiring environmental evaluation
and concrete measures to avoid negative impacts of port improvement for
projects approved through the credit line.
9.    Providing for the above measures through the small-ports Project
component would guarantee that ROCS-1 explicitly finances most
associated environmental costs. At the same time, it would strengthen
the capacity of CNMA to participate and opportunely provide inputs to
related development projects. This proposal was tentatively discussed



- 222 -
ANNEX 5-3
Page 4 of 4
with the Director of the CNA and his team during project appraisal, and
met with their support. Specific measures to facilitate implementation
of the above monitoring were reviewed, and discussions initiated with
other potential donors, particularly EEC, and UNEP. Contacts with the
forestry and fisheries agencies remain to be initiated. Concrete
measures proposed within the small-ports Project component in order to
meet the above requirements include providing: (i) initial assistance
to establish environmental monitoring capacity at the ports, in
particular training for port environmental monitoring agents; (ii) oil
receptor facilities in three strategically located ports; (iii) minimum
toilet facilities for port workers and passengers where required; and
(iv) assistance to develop CNA's capacity to review proposals presented
to the credit line.
C. LEGISLATION AND REGULATIONS
10.   Ports.  Existing port legislation and regulations regarding
environmental conservation and protection should be reviewed together
with port legislation studies, and complemented and redrafted to include
protection of estuary, near shore, and other coastal fisheries
(particular attention should be paid to conservation of their respective
habitats, especially spawning, breeding, and rearing areas); enforcement
should be reinstated for existing related legislation, and promptly
implemented for new legislation. All small port investments through
ROCS-1 and subsequent projects should comply with the International
Marine Pollution Convention - MARPOL 73/78 (MARPOL 73/78 Convention).
Its is advisable that this convention be adopted by GOM prior to a major
increase in traffic.
11.   Forestry.  It is strongly advised that legislation and regulations
regarding timber (including fuelwood) exploitation be reviewed by both
the Ministry of Agriculture and CNA to reflect sustainability in the
development and exploitation of forest and timber resources at the
local, as well as the national level. Enforcemcnt of existing
legislation and regulations should be strengthened, particularly the
issuing and control of permits for timber concessions.
D. TRAINING AND TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE
12.   Training and TA will be provided to strengthen CNA's, MTC's and
MCA's capabilities to support environmentally sound rehabilitation and
development of the country's roads and ports. CNA's training and TA is
scheduled to start up-front to ensure that the necessary support, plus
project-related environmental monitoring agents, are readily available
once other investments and civil works start. In view of the strategic
position of CNA and its overall responsibility to ensure environmentally
sound development of the country, it is crucial that it be staffed with
highly qualified manpower to provide environmental leadership to all
other Mozambican institutions.
